Hamd, Shukr, and Thana: Definitions and Distinctions
Defining and distinguishing between hamd, shukr, and thana'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hamd, shukr, and thana' and explain the Hanafi analysis of thana' as a kinayah.

Core Idea
Thana' is a kinayah (metonymy) for directing all praise to Allah, broader than hamd's verbal-only praise.

In this passage from a Hanafi usul commentary, the author defines three key terms related to praise and gratitude. Understanding these distinctions is essential for grasping the precise meanings of Quranic and hadith texts. The passage also introduces the rhetorical concept of kinayah, which is a key tool in Hanafi textual analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terms
List the three terms discussed: hamd, shukr, and thana'. Note that the passage focuses on their definitions and interrelations.
These terms appear frequently in Quran and hadith.
2
Understand the scope of each
Hamd is limited to verbal praise. Shukr encompasses heart, tongue, and limbs. Thana' is analyzed as a kinayah implying a broader intention of veneration.
The passage explicitly states that shukr is performed with heart, tongue, and limbs, while hamd is only with the tongue.
3
Analyze the argument for thana' as kinayah
The commentator argues that thana' is a kinayah because the phrase 'turning all praise towards Allah' is a necessary consequence (lazim) of the act of veneration, and it is used to imply the intention of veneration (malzum).
Kinayah in Hanafi usul is the use of a necessary implication to convey the intended meaning.
4
Contrast thana' with hamd
Thana' is not simply verbal praise like hamd; it is a rhetorical device that includes the intention of directing all forms of reverence to Allah.
The passage says that the general meaning of thana' cannot be performed by merely saying 'praising' (hamid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمام اشیاء کو اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف منعطف اور مائل کرنا مراد ہے تو یہ جمیع انواع عبادات کی طرف اشارہ ہوگا کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی نعمتیں مستوجب ہیں کہ ان پر شکر بالقلب واللسان والجوارح ادا کیا جائے اور حمد تو صرف لسانا ہوتا ہے باقی انواع شکر کو شامل نہیں تھا باقی رہا یہ سوال کہ ثناء بھی تعریف باللسان ہے جیسے حمد تو اس کا اندفاع یوں کیا جاتا ہے کہ یہ در حقیقت کنایہ ہے کیونکہ جو شخص بتصد تعظیم اپنی ان تمام اشیاء کو جو صالح للتعظیم ہیں اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف موڑتا ہے یہ ملزومات ہیں اور عنان الثناء الیہ ثانیا یہ اس کا لازم ہے تو اطلاق لازم ہوا اور ارادہ ملزوم یعنی قصد تعظیم بہذہ الاشیاء اور انتقال من اللازم الى الملزوم کو کنا یہ کہتے ہیں تو یہ مفہوم عمومی لعنان الثناء من جميع الجهات الیہ تعالیٰ ثانیاً ای صارف سے ادا ہو سکتا ہے۔ جو حامدا سے ادا نہیں ہو رہا تھا۔
If by 'turning all things towards Allah' is meant inclining them [to Him], then this would indicate all types of worship, because Allah's blessings oblige that gratitude be performed with the heart, tongue, and limbs. However, 'praise' (hamd) is only with the tongue, and it does not include the other types of gratitude. As for the remaining question that 'thana' is also praise with the tongue like hamd, its rebuttal is that [thana] is actually a metonymy (kinayah). This is because the person who turns all those things worthy of veneration towards Allah with a resolve to venerate—these are the implications (lazimat), and the expression 'turning the rein of praise towards Him, secondly' is its necessary consequence (lazim). Thus the term (lazim) is used, while intending the implication (malzum), i.e., the intention of veneration through these things. The transfer from the necessary to the implied is called metonymy (kinayah). So this general meaning of 'turning all directions of praise towards Allah, secondly' can be performed by the agent, which could not be performed by the one who merely says 'praising' (hamid).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage defines three related terms: hamd (praise), shukr (gratitude), and thana' (praise in a broader sense). The author explains that hamd is limited to verbal praise, while shukr encompasses verbal, mental, and physical gratitude. Thana' is analyzed as a metonymy (kinayah) where the phrase 'turning all praise towards Allah' is a necessary implication of the act of veneration. The commentator clarifies that thana' is not simply verbal praise like hamd; rather, it is a rhetorical device that implies directing all forms of reverence to Allah.

Key Terms
حمد (hamd): Verbal praise of Allah, distinct from shukr.
شكر (shukr): Gratitude expressed with heart, tongue, and limbs.
ثناء (thana'): Praise directed to Allah, used as a metonymy for the act of veneration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly describes thana' according to the passage?
A) It is identical to hamd, both being verbal praise.
B) It is a metonymy implying the direction of all praise to Allah.
C) It is a physical act of worship.
D) It is limited to gratitude of the heart.

Key Takeaway
Thana' is a kinayah representing the comprehensive direction of all veneration to Allah, distinct from the merely verbal hamd.

Combining Haqiqah and Majaz in One Word
Resolving the problem of combining literal and metaphorical meanings in one word.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul prohibits combining literal and metaphorical meanings in a single word usage and apply the resolution of assuming separate omitted words.

Core Idea
A single word cannot bear both haqiqah and majaz at once; they must be from distinct words.

In this passage, the author addresses a potential objection to a particular interpretation of the word 'hamid' (praising) in the basmalah. The objector argues that if 'hamid' is taken literally in one context and metaphorically in another, it would combine haqiqah and majaz in the same word, which is invalid. The author responds by showing that the second instance involves an omitted word, so no combination occurs. This illustrates a fundamental principle of Hanafi usul: a single word usage cannot simultaneously convey literal and metaphorical meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The opponent states that the third interpretation leads to using 'hamid' literally for worldly praise and metaphorically for intention of praise in the afterlife, thus combining haqiqah and majaz.
2
Understand the basis for invalidity
In Hanafi usul, a word can only have one meaning (literal or metaphorical) in a single usage. If both are intended, the usage is invalid.
This is a core rule: al-jam' bayn al-haqiqah wa al-majaz fi lafdh wahid bāṭil.
3
Examine the author's response
The author asserts that in the second instance, the word 'hamid' is not the same; an omitted word meaning 'intending' is understood. Therefore, the literal and metaphorical meanings come from separate words.
The omitted word is implied by taqdīr (estimation).
4
Apply the principle to the text
The original phrase is reconstructed as 'praising Allah first and praising (intending) secondly.' This avoids combining haqiqah and majaz in one word.
5
Conclude the resolution
The objection is refuted, and the third interpretation stands valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قلت على الوجه الثالث یعنی وجہ ثالث جس کے اندر حامدًا اولاً سے حمد فی الدنیا اور ثانیاً سے فی الآخرۃ مراد ہے اس سے لازم آتا ہے کہ حامدا ایک ہی لفظ ہے اولا کی صورت میں اس سے حمد بالفعل مراد ہو گا جو ابتدا ر کتاب کے ساتھ مقترن ہے اور ثانیاً کے اندر اس حامد ا سے حمد بالفعل مراد نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ حمد اخروی ابتدار بالکتاب کے ساتھ مقترن نہیں ہو سکتا حالانکہ حال کے لئے مقارنت مع العامل شرط ہے تو لا محالہ ثانیا میں اسی حامد ا سے نادیا و عازما علی الحمد مراد ہو گی تو ایک ہی لفظ سے بیک وقت حقیقت اور مجاز مراد ہوا کیونکہ حمد بالفعل حامدا کا حقیقی معنی ہے اور عزم علی الحمد حمد کا مجازی مفہوم ہو سکتا ہے تو یہ جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز ہے جو باطل ہے قلت يجعل اب خلاصہ جواب یہ کہ ثانیا کے ساتھ اور لفظ حامدا محذوف ہے جو کہ بمعنی نادیا و عاز ما علی الحمد ہے اصل عبارت یوں ہوگی حامدا اللہ تعالیٰ اولاً وحامدا ثانيا لہذا ایک ہی لفظ سے حقیقت اور مجاز مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ الگ الگ لفظ سے ہے ۔
If you say: 'According to the third interpretation, i.e., the third aspect in which 'hamid' first refers to praise in this world and secondly to praise in the afterlife, this necessitates that 'hamid' is one word. In the first case, it means actual praise which is simultaneous with the beginning of the book. In the second case, this same 'hamid' cannot mean actual praise because eschatological praise cannot be simultaneous with the beginning of the book, while for the hal, simultaneity with the factor is a condition. So inevitably, in the second case, this same 'hamid' must mean intent and resolve upon praise. Then from one word, both literal (actual praise) and metaphorical (intent) meanings are intended simultaneously. This is a combination of literal and metaphorical usage, which is invalid.' I say: 'It can be...' The summary of the answer is that with the second [instance], another word 'hamid' is omitted, which means intent and resolve upon praise. So the original expression would be: 'praising Allah first and praising [intending] secondly.' Therefore, literal and metaphorical meanings are not intended from the same word, but from separate words.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage resolves a logical objection. The third interpretation of 'hamid' in the basmalah (first: praise in this world, second: praise in the afterlife) leads to a problem: if the same word 'hamid' is used literally in the first instance (actual praise) and metaphorically in the second (intention of praise), it would combine literal and metaphorical usage, which is invalid. The answer is that in the second instance, the word 'hamid' is not the same; an omitted word is understood to mean 'intending praise', so they are two different words, avoiding the combination.

Key Terms
حقيقة (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word as conventionally established.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical or transferred meaning of a word.
تقدير (taqdīr): The analytical assumption of an omitted word or phrase to complete the meaning of a text, often used to resolve apparent contradictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the objector consider the third interpretation invalid?
A) Because the hal condition is not met.
B) Because it combines literal and metaphorical meanings in one word.
C) Because the word 'hamid' is not appropriate.
D) Because the basmalah is not mentioned.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a single word cannot simultaneously convey literal and metaphorical meanings; if a text seems to require both, the interpreter must assume separate words (taqdīr) to avoid the combination.

Reason for Sending Salutations and the Rhetoric of Description
Explaining why praise is followed by salutations on the best of messengers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two reasons for not explicitly naming the Prophet in the salutation and explain the rhetorical device of majaz mursal in the context of Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The Prophet is honored by description, not name; the greatest blessing, Islam, came through him.

In this passage, the commentator provides a justification for the structure of the salutation. After praising Allah, the author sends blessings upon the Prophet, but does not name him explicitly. The commentator explains the rationale, and also clarifies a metaphor regarding racehorses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
State that the salutation follows praise because Islam, the greatest blessing, reached us through the Prophet's intermediation.
2
Analyze the omission of explicit naming
Note the two reasons given: (1) to honor the Prophet by using a description, and (2) because the description 'the best of messengers' is unambiguous.
The commentator says great persons are not named; their attributes suffice.
3
Understand the rhetorical device
Explain the term 'majaz mursal' as used in the horse race analogy: the condition (racecourse) is mentioned to denote the location (the horses).
The text says 'al-halbat' is used figuratively for the racecourse.
4
Connect to usul al-fiqh
Relate the use of description to the Hanafi concept of 'amm and khass: a description that is specific enough can function like a proper name.
This shows how clarity in identification can be achieved without explicit naming.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى افضل رسله مصليا لما كان الحمد کے بعد صلوۃ علی الرسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لے آنے کی وجہ پیش کر رہا ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی جانب سے جو نعمتیں عباد تک موصول ہوئی ہیں ان سے افضل و اعظم نعمت دین الاسلام ہے کیونکہ اس ہی کے ذریعہ دنیاوی کامیابی کے علاوہ دار السلام کی نعمتوں تک وصول حاصل ہو گا اور یہی دین اسلام عباد تک رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ذریعہ اور توسط سے موصول ہوا ہے لہذا ضروری ہے کہ بعد الحمد رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے حق میں صلوۃ و دعا پیش کی جائے اس لئے محمد کے بعد صلوۃ پیش کی دنی ترك التصريح از مصنف کے نزدیک جو نسخہ توضیح مقروہ اور مقررہ ہے اس میں رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے اسم مقدس کی تصریح نہیں ہے صرف افضل رسلہ کی وصف مذکور ہے تو اس ترک تصریح کے شارح نے دو وجوہ پیش کئے ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ تنوید بشانهای تعظیم بشانه یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی عظمت شان کو ظاہر کرنے کی خاطر تصریح بالاسم ترک کر دی کیونکہ اولو العظیم اور صاحب عظمت حضرات کا نام نہیں لیا جاتا بلکہ اوصاف جلیلہ کے ذکرہ کو کافی سمجھا جاتا ہے۔ ثانیاً یہ کہ تنبیہ یعنی اس امر پر تنبیہ کرنا مقصود ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا افضل الرسل ہونا ایک امر واضح اور جلی ہے جو کسی ایک پر مخفی نہیں لہذا اس وصف سے کسی غیر کی طرف ذہن جا ہی نہیں سکتا اور تصریح بالاسم کے تعیین کی ضرورت وہاں ہوتی ہے جہاں وصف کے ساتھ مقصود کے سمجھنے میں اشتباہ ہو جب یہاں اشتباہ نہیں بلکہ یہ وصف رسول الله صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لئے متعین فی العرف ہے اس لئے تصریح بالاسم ضروری نہیں ہے و الحلبة الم یعنی طلبہ ان گھوڑوں کو کہا جاتا جو مختلف اطراف سے میدان میں مسابقت اور دوڑ میں مقابلہ کرنے کے لئے جمع کئے جاتے ہیں لیکن یہاں بطور مجاز مرسل کے مضمار یعنی وہ میدان مراد ہے جس میں گھوڑے دوڑائے جا نہیں علی طریقہ اطلاق الحال واراده المحل والمعنى هو السابق مصنف نے جو مجلیا و مصلیا کہا ہے اس کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ محلی اس فرس کو کہتے ہیں جو میدان دوڑ میں سب گھوڑوں سے آگے نکل جائے اور مصلی اس کو کہتے جو اس سابق فرس کے ساتھ پیچھے رہے اس قدر کہ راسه ای رأس المصلی عند صلوه
And upon the best of His messengers sending blessings. Since after praise, the reason for bringing salutations upon the Messenger (peace be upon him) is mentioned. The summary is: Among the blessings received by servants from Allah, the greatest and most excellent blessing is the religion of Islam, because through it, in addition to worldly success, one attains the blessings of the abode of peace. And this religion of Islam reached the servants through the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his intermediation. Therefore, it is necessary that after praise, salutations and prayers be offered for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Hence, salutations are offered after Muhammad. Regarding the omission of explicit mention by the author: according to the version of al-Tawdih that is read and established, the holy name of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is not explicitly mentioned; only the description 'the best of His messengers' is given. The commentator gives two reasons for this omission of explicit mention. First: to show reverence for his high status—because great and majestic persons are not named, rather mentioning their lofty attributes is considered sufficient. Second: to point out that the fact that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is the best of messengers is a clear and manifest matter, hidden from no one. Therefore, this description cannot direct the mind to anyone else. The need for explicit naming is where there is ambiguity in understanding the intended person through description. Since there is no ambiguity here, and this description is conventionally determined for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), explicit naming is not necessary. 'And al-halbat al-mu' means: horses brought together from various sides to compete in the racecourse. But here, by way of majaz mursal, 'mudmar' is intended, meaning the racecourse. The expression follows the pattern of using the condition for the location. And the meaning is 'the forerunner.' The author said 'muhalli' and 'musalli'. In explanation, he said: 'muhalli' is called a horse that outruns all others in the racecourse, and 'musalli' is called one that stays behind the forerunner such that its head is at the place of the salat (prayer) of the forerunner.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage explains why the author of the matn sends salutations upon the Prophet after praising Allah. The greatest blessing is Islam, which was transmitted through the Prophet. Then two reasons are given for not explicitly naming the Prophet: to honor him by using a description instead, and because it is obvious that 'the best of messengers' refers to him. Finally, the author explains the terms 'muhalli' and 'musalli' from the original text, which refer to horses in a race: the forerunner and the one that follows.

Key Terms
صلوٰۃ (salah): Prayer; in this context, supplication and blessing upon the Prophet.
مجاز مرسل (majaz mursal): A type of metaphorical usage where the condition (hal) is used to denote the location (mahall).
محلی (muhalli): A horse that comes first in a race, the forerunner.
مصلی (musalli): A horse that follows the forerunner closely, with its head at the forerunner's place of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the main reason for not explicitly naming the Prophet in the salutation?
A) The name was forgotten.
B) To show reverence and because the description is clear.
C) The text was abbreviated due to space.
D) The author disliked mentioning names.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet is honored by description, not name; the greatest blessing, Islam, came through him.

Understanding Compound Analogy (Tashbih Murakkab) in Usul Discourse
Explains the compound analogy likening scholars to horses in a race

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of a compound analogy (tashbih murakkab) used in usul texts, explain its purpose in illustrating scholarly hierarchy, and apply the terms mujalli, musalli, and masbuq to describe relative positions.

Core Idea
A compound analogy uses a vivid image—like a horse race—to make abstract scholarly rankings concrete.

In usul al-fiqh, authors often employ rhetorical devices to clarify their place in the scholarly tradition. This passage from al-Tawdih uses a compound analogy (tashbih murakkab) drawn from a horse race: the author compares himself to a leading horse (mujalli) and others to followers (musalli) or those behind (masbuq). Understanding this analogy not only reveals the author's self-assessment but also introduces a key rhetorical tool used throughout Hanafi usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the analogy's components
List the elements of the analogy: the field (racecourse), the horses (scholars), and the hierarchy (mujalli, musalli, masbuq).
2
Define the key terms
Understand the meanings: mujalli = the leading horse (premier scholar), musalli = the follower (second tier), masbuq = those left behind (lesser scholars).
3
Relate to author's self-positioning
The author places himself as mujalli and musalli—both leader and follower? Or he leads and follows? Actually, he claims the top position (mujalli) and acknowledges others as followers or behind.
This reflects scholarly humility combined with authority.
4
Recognize the rhetorical type
This is a tashbih murakkab (compound analogy) because it combines multiple elements (horses, positions) into a single comparative image.
Also called tashbih mu'allaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے اس کو تشبیہ دی گئی ہے اس ہیئتہ منتزعہ کے ساتھ جو ماخوذ ہے اس میدان مسابقت سے جس میں مختلف گھوڑے دوڑ رہے ہیں کوئی مجلی ہے اور کوئی مصلی اور کچھ اس سے پیچھے بھی ہوں گے اسی طرح مصنف نے اپنے آپ کو مجلی اور مصلی قرار دیا اور دوسروں کو مسبوق یہ ہے تمثیل جس کو تشبیہ مرکب اور مؤلف بھی کہتے ہیں۔
It has been likened to this extracted form which is taken from the field of competition in which different horses are running—some are mujallī (the leader) and some are musallī (the follower) and some are behind them. Similarly, the author has placed himself as mujallī and musallī and others as masbūq (lagging behind). This is an example which is called compound analogy (tashbīh murakkab) and also composite.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage discusses the author's use of a compound analogy to describe his position relative to other scholars. The analogy likens the field of scholarship to a racecourse where horses compete. The leading horse is called mujallī, the one following is musallī, and those further behind are masbūq. The author of al-Tawḍīḥ (the matn) presents himself as the leader (mujallī) and others as followers or behind. This type of analogy is known as tashbīh murakkab (compound analogy) or tashbīh mu'allaf (composite analogy) in Arabic rhetoric. It is used to make the abstract hierarchy more concrete.

Key Terms
تشبیہ مرکب (tashbīh murakkab): A compound analogy that combines multiple elements to create a comparative image, used here to depict scholarly hierarchy.
مجلی (mujallī): The leading horse in the race; metaphorically, the foremost scholar or authority.
مصلی (musallī): The follower or second horse; metaphorically, a scholar who follows closely behind the leader.
مسبوق (masbūq): One who is left behind; metaphorically, a scholar of lesser rank or later generation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the compound analogy from this passage, the term 'masbūq' refers to which group?
A) The author himself
B) The leading horses
C) Scholars who are behind the author in rank
D) All participants in the race

Key Takeaway
A compound analogy (tashbih murakkab) uses a familiar scene to clarify hierarchical relationships, a tool often found in Hanafi usul works to position authors relative to the scholarly tradition.

Taqdīm: When Advancement Means Emphasis, Not Restriction
Clarifies two functions of taqdīm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when taqdīm (advancement) indicates restriction (ḥaṣr) versus emphasis (ta'kīd) in Hanafi textual analysis.

Core Idea
Advancement (taqdīm) is not always for restriction; it may be for emphasis or honor.

In this passage, the commentator unfolds a subtle usul point: although some advancements in Arabic sentences signal restriction (ḥaṣr), others are purely for emphasis and honor. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting legal texts. The commentary uses two examples—one where taqdīm is restrictive, and another where it is emphatic—to illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of taqdīm discussed
Locate where the commentator distinguishes between taqdīm that is for restriction (e.g., 'إلیہ ثانیًا') and taqdīm that is for emphasis (e.g., 'على أفضل الرسل' and 'في حلبة الصلوات').
The key is the presence or absence of a qarīna (clue) that would otherwise require restriction.
2
Analyze the evidence for each type
The commentator provides reasoning: for the restrictive taqdīm, the meaning shifts to exclusivity; for the emphatic taqdīm, the broader context shows that other alternatives are not excluded (e.g., other prophets deserve salutations, competition extends beyond prayers).
The Quranic verse 'سَابِقُوا إِلَى مَغْفِرَةٍ' supports the broad application.
3
Apply the principle to new examples
Given a sentence with taqdīm, determine whether it indicates restriction or emphasis by checking if the advancement excludes other possibilities.
If excluding others would contradict known rulings or texts, the taqdīm is likely for emphasis.
4
Contrast with a hypothetical restrictive taqdīm
Imagine how the sentence would be structured if restriction were intended (e.g., using 'إلا' or 'إنما'). Compare with the given examples to reinforce the distinction.
This step builds practical awareness of how ḥaṣr mechanisms differ from mere taqdīm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقدیم المعمولات او قرائن ثلث سے الیہ ثانیا کو مستثنیٰ کرنا پڑے گا کیونکہ وہ تقدیم مصر کے لئے ہے جیسے کہ شارح نے اس کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ ینبغی ان یعرض عن جانب الخلق ويصرف اعنة الثناء من جميع الجهات الى جانب الحق تعالى وتقدس عالما بانه المستحق للثناء وحدة البته علی افضل رسلہ کی تقدیم اور اسی طرح فی حلبتہ الصلوات کی تقدیم حصر کے لئے نہیں ہے کیونکہ افضل الرسل علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کے علاوہ باقی انہیار کے اسمائے گرامی پر علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کہنا پڑتا ہے اور اسی طرح صرف حلبة الصلوات کے اندر بھی مسابقت نہیں بلکہ باقی خیرات وحسنات کے اندر مسابقت ہونی چاہئیے ۔ سَابِقُوا إِلى مَغْفِرَةٍ مِنْ تَكُوا الا یہ تو یہ تقدیمات صرف مجمع بندی اور اہتمام مقام کی غرض سے ہیں۔
The advancement of objects or from the three clues, excluding 'إلیہ ثانیًا' is necessary because that advancement is for restriction, as the commentator explained: 'It is appropriate to turn away from the side of creation and direct the reins of praise from all directions to the side of al-Ḥaqq (the Truth), knowing that He alone deserves praise without any associate.' Also, the advancement of 'ʿalā afḍal al-rusul' and similarly 'fī ḥalbat al-ṣalawāt' is not for restriction because besides afḍal al-rusul (the best of messengers), on the names of other prophets, saying 'alayhi al-ṣalāt wa al-salām' is necessary. Similarly, competition is not only within the racecourse of prayers but should be in other good deeds. 'Race towards forgiveness from your Lord' – rather these advancements are only for the purpose of emphasizing and honoring the station.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains a subtle usul point about the advancement (taqdīm) of certain expressions in the author's wording. The commentator clarifies that when we advance a phrase like 'إلیہ ثانیًا' (to Him secondly), it is for the purpose of restriction (ḥaṣr), meaning that praise is exclusively for Allah. However, the advancement of ''alā afḍal al-rusul' (upon the best of messengers) and 'fī ḥalbat al-ṣalawāt' (in the racecourse of prayers) is not for restriction. The reason is that other prophets also deserve salutations, and competition is not limited to prayers but extends to all good deeds. The verse 'سَابِقُوا إِلَى مَغْفِرَةٍ' (Race towards forgiveness) supports this broad competition. Therefore, the taqdīm here is merely for emphasis and honor, not to restrict.

Key Terms
تقدیم (taqdīm): The syntactic advancement of a word or phrase in a sentence, here discussed as serving either restriction or emphasis.
حصر (ḥaṣr): A rhetorical device that restricts the predicate to the subject; in this passage, it contrasts with mere emphasis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Prophet is the only one worthy of praise.
D) Because the verse 'سَابِقُوا' restricts competition to prayers.

Key Takeaway
Taqdīm in Arabic can signal either restriction or emphasis; the deciding factor is whether the alternative would contradict known rulings or texts.

Distinguishing Adjectival and Adverbial 'Awwal' via Tanwīn
Explains the grammatical rule for tanwīn on 'awwalan' as an adverb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the adjectival and adverbial usage of the word 'awwal' based on the presence or absence of tanwīn and state the resulting semantic difference.

Core Idea
Tanwīn on 'awwal' marks adverbial meaning (before); without it, it is adjectival (first).

In usul al-fiqh, precise textual interpretation is crucial. A single grammatical marker like tanwīn can change the legal implication of a report. This lesson examines the case of 'awwalan' — when it takes tanwīn and when it does not, and what each usage means, as explained by the commentator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and the objection
Locate the word 'awwal' in the passage and understand the objection that as an ism tafḍīl it should be ghayr munṣarif (not taking tanwīn).
The objection assumes all uses of 'awwal' are adjectival.
2
Recognize the commentator's response
Note that the commentator distinguishes between adjectival and adverbial usage. When 'awwal' is used as an adverb (ẓarf) meaning 'before', it is not a superlative and thus takes tanwīn.
The key is the syntactic function, not the form of the word.
3
Apply the two usages to the examples
Analyze the given examples: 'laqītuhu 'āman awwal' (no tanwīn) vs 'laqītuhu 'āman awwalan' (with tanwīn). Determine the meaning in each case.
4
Derive the semantic difference
Conclude that without tanwīn it means 'the first year (of this year)', while with tanwīn it means 'a year before (this year)'.
The adverbial use implies a prior, non-specific time.
5
Connect to usul al-fiqh
Reflect on how grammatical precision affects the interpretation of legal texts, such as hadith or juristic statements, where similar distinctions may alter rulings.
This principle is used in usul to determine the precise meaning of words in sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان انتصاب اولا وثانياً یعنی اولاً و ثانیا اس مقام پر منصوب على الظرفیہ ہیں یعنی فی الاوقات الاولية والثانوية - واما التنوين في اولاً یہ جواب ہے اس اشکال کا کہ لفظ اول اسم تفضیل ہے جیسے کہ شارح نے اس کے نظائر سے استدلال کیا ہے تو اس وقت لفظ اول میں وصفیہ اور وزن فعل موجود ہے تو غیر منصرف ہوگا تو اس پر تنوین کا لانا کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے تو اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا لانه ظرف یعنی یہ وصفیہ کے معنی میں نہیں بلکہ بطور ظرفیہ کے مذکو ہے جو بمعنی قبل کے ہے یہی مراد ہے صحاح کی کہ جب اس کو بطور وصفیہ کے استعمال کیا جائے تو اس کو غیر منصرف کیا جائے گا اور کہا جائے گا لقیتہ عاما اول اور جب اس کو صفہ قرار نہ دیا جائے بلکہ ظرفیہ کے طور پر استعمال ہو تو منصرف ہو گا اور کہا جائے گا لقیتہ عاما اولاً بالتنوین پہلی صورت میں اس کا معنی ہوگا اول من هاذا العام یعنی اس سال کی بنسبت جو پہلا ہے اور ثانی صورت میں معنیٰ ہوگا قبل هاذا العام یعنی اس سال سے سابقہ مدت میں مثلاً اس وقت سال چودہ سو آٹھ ہجری ہے تو پہلی صورت کے لحاظ سے اول من هذا العام مراد ہو گا یعنی صرف چودہ سو سات ہجری اور ثانی صورت میں قبل هذا العام یعنی اس سال سے پہلے والے برس خواہ وہ سات ہو یا چھ ہو یا پاسخ و چار جو اس سابقہ مدت میں گزر چکے ہیں تعیین نہیں ہے ۔
And that the nasb (accusative) of 'awwalan' and 'thāniyan' means that 'awwalan' and 'thāniyan' here are in the accusative as adverbs, i.e., in the primary and secondary times. As for the tanwīn on 'awwalan', this is the answer to the objection that the word 'awwal' is a superlative noun, as the commentator argued by analogy with its counterparts. At that time, 'awwal' has a descriptive quality and the form of a verb, so it would be non-declinable (ghayr munṣarif). So how can tanwīn be correctly used on it? The answer is that it is an adverb, i.e., it is not used in the sense of a description but is mentioned as an adverb meaning 'before'. This is the meaning of al-Ṣiḥāḥ: when it is used as a description, it is made non-declinable, and one says 'laqītuhu 'āman awwal', and when it is not made a description but used as an adverb, it becomes declinable, and one says 'laqītuhu 'āman awwalan' with tanwīn. In the first case, the meaning is 'the first of this year', and in the second case, the meaning is 'before this year'.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses a grammatical objection regarding the tanwīn on 'awwalan'. Critics argue that 'awwal' is a superlative noun (ism tafḍīl) and should be non-declinable (ghayr munṣarif). The commentator refutes this by distinguishing its usage: when used as an adjective (ṣifah), it is indeed non-declinable, but when used as an adverb (ẓarf) meaning 'before', it is declinable and thus takes tanwīn. Two examples illustrate the semantic difference: 'āman awwal' means 'the first year (of the current year)' while 'āman awwalan' means 'a year before (the current year)'. This grammatical point is relevant to understanding the nuance in the author's wording.

Key Terms
تنوین (tanwīn): The nunation marking indefiniteness; here it distinguishes adverbial use from adjectival use.
غیر منصرف (ghayr munṣarif): A noun that does not accept tanwīn due to a reason such as being a superlative; here 'awwal' is not ghayr munṣarif when used adverbially.
ظرف (ẓarf): Adverb of time or place; in this lesson, 'awwal' as an adverb meaning 'before'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) I met him a year before
B) I met him the first year of this year
C) I met him last year
D) I met him many years ago

Key Takeaway
The presence or absence of tanwīn on 'awwal' signals whether it functions as an adjective (first) or an adverb (before), affecting the interpretation of temporal references.

Īhām (Amphiboly) in Usul: Interpreting 'Sa'ada Jadduhu'
Defines īhām and applies it to a phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify īhām in a textual source and apply the Hanafi principle of contextual interpretation (qarina) to resolve mushtarak words.

Core Idea
When a word has two meanings, context determines which is intended—whether near or far.

Īhām (amphiboly) is a rhetorical device where a word carries two meanings, and the less obvious one is intended. In usul al-fiqh, this concept helps us interpret ambiguous (mushtarak) words in scripture. The phrase 'sa'ada jadduhu' from supplications exemplifies this: 'jadd' can mean grandfather (near) or fortune (far), but context points to fortune. Understanding īhām sharpens your ability to weigh contextual clues in textual analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its dual meanings
Locate the word 'jadd' in the phrase. Note that it has two distinct meanings: one near (grandfather) and one far (fortune). This is the essence of īhām.
The 'near' meaning is the most common or literal; the 'far' meaning is less common but contextually appropriate.
2
Examine the context
The phrase occurs in a supplication (dua). Supplications typically seek blessings or good fortune, not exaltation of a grandfather. Thus, context favors the far meaning.
Context (qarina) is the key tool for disambiguation.
3
Classify the word in usul
In Hanafi usul, words with multiple meanings are called mushtarak (homonym). The principle governing mushtarak is that interpretation requires a qarina (contextual indication).
Hanafi scholars treat mushtarak as zanni al-dalala until clarified by qarina.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
Using the qarina of supplication, the intended meaning is 'fortune' (the far meaning). This yields the correct interpretation: 'may his fortune be elevated'.
This aligns with the technical definition of īhām: intending the far meaning.
5
Note the common understanding
The passage notes that common usage (muta'ārif 'ind al-'āmmah) defines īhām simply as using a word with two meanings where one is intended, without requiring nearness or distance. This broader view is accepted in rhetoric.
In usul, we adhere to the technical definition that requires the far meaning for īhām.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سعد جدہ فیه ایهام فن بدیع میں ایہام اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ ایسا لفظ ذکر کیا جائے جس کے دو معنی ہوں ایک قریب اور دوسرا بعید اور مراد بعید ہو تو کہا جاتا ہے کہ جد کا معنی ابو الاب قریبی ہے اور بخت بعیدی اور یہاں بمعنی بخت ہے کیونکہ یہ مقام دعا ہے اس لئے معنی بخت مراد ہونا چاہیئے اور متعارف عند العامہ یہ ہے کہ ایسا لفظ استعمال کیا جائے جس کے دو معنیٰ ہوں اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک مطلقا مراد ہو قرب و بعد کا سوال عند العامہ نہیں تو پھر اس عبادت کا محمول علی الایہام ہونا ظاہر ہے ۔
'Sa'ada jadduhu' contains īhām. In badīʿ (rhetoric), īhām is when a word is mentioned that has two meanings, one near and one far, and the far meaning is intended. It is said that 'jadd' means grandfather (near) and fortune (far). Here it is used in the sense of fortune because this is a place of supplication, so the meaning of fortune should be intended. And the common understanding (muta'ārif 'ind al-'āmmah) is that such a word is used with two meanings, one of which is absolutely intended, without consideration of nearness and distance. So, this invocation being carried upon īhām is evident.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage defines the rhetorical figure īhām (amphiboly) and applies it to the phrase 'sa'ada jadduhu' (may his fortune be elevated). The author explains that 'jadd' has a near meaning (grandfather) and a far meaning (fortune). In the context of a supplication, the far meaning (fortune) is intended, which constitutes īhām. The passage also notes a common understanding among the general public that īhām simply uses a word with two meanings, one of which is intended, without concern for nearness or distance degrees. This is relevant to usul al-fiqh because understanding such rhetorical devices helps interpret authoritative texts correctly.

Key Terms
ایہام (īhām): A rhetorical figure where a word with two meanings is used, and the less obvious (far) meaning is intended.
مشترک (mushtarak): A word that has multiple meanings (homonym).
قرینہ (qarina): Contextual indicator that clarifies the intended meaning of an ambiguous word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Tasāmuh vs Taḍmīn: Interpreting Grammatical Anomalies in Usul Texts
Linguistic analysis of a grammatical anomaly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasāmuh and taḍmīn as interpretive devices in Hanafi usul, and apply them to explain anomalous grammatical constructions in authoritative texts.

Core Idea
Taḍmīn is preferred over tasāmuh because it preserves both meanings without mixing literal and metaphorical usage.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a linguistic anomaly in the author's invocation: the verb 'wafaqa' normally takes 'lām', but the author uses 'bā''. Rather than dismissing this as mere laxity (tasāmuh), the commentator invokes taḍmīn, where the verb implicitly carries a secondary meaning. This reflects a broader usul principle: we prefer interpretations that maintain precision and avoid unnecessary figurative language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic anomaly
The verb 'wafaqa' is normally transitive with the preposition 'lām' (e.g., wafaqahu Allāh), but the author uses it with 'bā'' (wafaqanī Allāh al-tawfīq bi...). Identify this deviation as the starting point of analysis.
The anomaly is the unexpected preposition.
2
Understand the two proposed explanations
The text offers two possibilities: tasāmuh (using a word in a non-literal sense without proper relationship or indication) and taḍmīn (implying another verb, here 'sharrafanī', so the 'bā'' belongs to the implied verb). Grasp the key difference: tasāmuh relies on loose understanding, taḍmīn maintains a literal core while adding a secondary meaning.
Tasāmuh is akin to metaphorical laxity; taḍmīn is a precise linguistic device.
3
Analyze the commentator's preference
The commentator prefers taḍmīn because it avoids 'jam' bayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz' (combining literal and metaphorical). Taḍmīn allows the verb to retain its real meaning while implicitly conveying a second meaning through the preposition.
This preference is based on the principle that authoritative texts should be interpreted in the most consistent and precise manner.
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
In usul, when encountering a grammatical irregularity in a foundational text (e.g., a Quran verse, hadith, or matn), always first attempt a taḍmīn-based interpretation before resorting to tasāmuh. This aligns with the broader Hanafi avoidance of unnecessary figurative language.
The principle is: al-asl fi al-kalam al-haqiqah – the default is literal meaning; taḍmīn preserves haqiqah.

Source Text

وفقني الله التوفيق جعل الاسباب موافقة اصطلاح شریعت میں موافقت للمطلوب الخیر کی قید کی جاتی ہے اگر مطلوب شر کے اسباب مہیا اور متوافق ہو جائیں تو اصطلاح شریعت میں اسے خذلان کہتے ہیں اس لئے و فقہم اللہ کے مقابلہ میں خذ لہم اللہ کہا جاتا ہے و يعدى باللام یعنی مفعول ثانی کی طرف اس کا تعدیہ باللام ہوتا ہے نہ کہ بالیا، مصنف نے یہاں اسے متعدی بالباء کیا ہے تو یہ تعدیہ یا تو مبنی علی التسامح ہے یا علی التضمين لمعنی التشریف ای شرفنی اللہ تعالیٰ تالیف تسامح کا معنی ایک لفظ کو معنی حقیقی کے غیر میں استعمال کرنا بغیر کسی علاقہ مقبولہ کے اور بغیر قرینہ دالہ کے صرف اعتماد علی ظہورالفہم ہوتا ہے اور تضمین یہ ہوتی ہے کہ ایک لفظ ذکر کر کے اس کے ساتھ حقیقی معنیٰ مراد لیا جائے اور اس کے ساتھ ایک دوسرا معنیٰ تبعا لفظ آخرہ کے ساتھ مراد ہو جو وہ مذکور نہیں صرف اس کا متعلق اور صلہ ذکر کر کے اس محذوف پر دلالت کرائی جاتی ہے جیسے یہاں وفتنی سے حقیقی معنی توفیق کا مراد ہے لیکن اس کے تابع معنی تشریف بلفظ شرفنی بھی مراد ہے جو غیر مذکور ہے۔ اس پر صرف اس کا صلہ یعنی حرف بالا کر دلالت کرائی گئی ہے اس کا فائدہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ایک لفظ کے ساتھ دو معنیٰ کا فائدہ حاصل ہو جاتا ہے لیکن دوسرا لفظ ضمنا مراد ضرور ہوتا ہے تاکہ ایک ہی لفظ کے ساتھ جمع بین الحقيقة والمجاز لازم نہ آئے ۔ کثیر ا ما يتسامح الم اس تسامح پر بلا وجہ محمول کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جبکہ باب تضمین بہت وسیع ہے کما قال ابن جینی " لو نقلت تضمینات العرب لاجتمعت مجلدات “ ہاں اگر کہیں تضمین نہ ہو سکے تو مجبور ا تسامح پر محمول کیا جائے گا لہذا شارح کا تسامح بالكثرة کا الزام على المصنف بلاوجہ ہے
'Wafaqanī Allāh al-tawfīq' means making causes agree. In Shariʿah terminology, agreement is qualified with the desired good. If causes for an evil desired are prepared and aligned, then in Shariʿah terminology that is called khidhlān. Therefore, in contrast to 'wafaqahum Allāh', it is said 'khadhalahum Allāh'. It is transitive with 'lām' (i.e., its transitivity to the second object is with lām, not with 'alif). The author here made it transitive with 'bā'' so either this transitivity is based on tasāmuh (tolerance/inaccuracy) or on taḍmīn (conceptual inclusion) with the meaning of tashrīf (honoring) i.e., 'sharrafanī Allāh taʿālā'. Tasāmuh means using a word in other than its real meaning without an accepted relationship and without a clear indication, relying only on understanding. Taḍmīn means mentioning a word with its real meaning intended but simultaneously intending a secondary meaning implicitly through another word not mentioned, and the existence of that secondary word is indicated by the preposition. The benefit is that two meanings are achieved with one word, but the second word is implicitly intended to avoid combining literal and metaphoric usage. It is said that tasāmuh is frequent, but there is no need to attribute it without reason when the door of taḍmīn is wide.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the linguistic choices in the author's invocation 'wafaqanī Allāh al-tawfīq'. It first defines tawfīq (divine assistance towards good) and khidhlān (abandonment towards evil). The verb 'wafaqa' is normally transitive with 'lām', but the author uses it with 'bā''. Two explanations are offered: either tasāmuh (a loose usage without proper relationship) or taḍmīn (where the verb implies another verb, here 'sharrafanī', and the 'bā'' is the preposition of that implied verb). The commentator prefers taḍmīn because it avoids mixing literal and metaphorical use. A quote from Ibn Jinnī emphasizes the broad scope of taḍmīn. This is a classic usul discussion of how to interpret anomalous grammatical constructions in authoritative texts.

Key Terms
توفیق (tawfīq): Divine assistance making causes align for the desired good
خذلان (khidhlān): Divine abandonment when causes align for evil
تسامح (tasāmuh): Using a word in a non-literal sense without proper rhetorical relationship or indication
تضمین (taḍmīn): Using one verb to imply another verb, achieving two meanings with one word

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator prefer taḍmīn over tasāmuh as the explanation for the author's use of 'ب' with 'وَفَقَنِي'?
A) Because tasāmuh is not permissible in the Arabic language
B) Because taḍmīn allows two meanings without mixing literal and figurative usage
C) Because the author explicitly stated taḍmīn
D) Because tasāmuh would imply the author made a grammatical error

Key Takeaway
Taḍmīn is the preferred Hanafi interpretive device for grammatical anomalies in authoritative texts, as it preserves literal meaning while adding secondary meaning.

Linguistic Analysis of 'كلم' as a Singular Genus Noun in Hanafi Usul
Addressing the objection on basmalah and analyzing 'كلم' as a singular genus noun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify 'كلم' as a singular noun of genus and explain why it takes a masculine adjective, applying the Hanafi usul principle that genus nouns are lexically singular.

Core Idea
The word 'كلم' in 'الكلم الطيب' is a singular genus noun—its masculine adjective proves it is not a plural.

This lesson tackles a common objection concerning the pronoun referent in the opening of a text and then dives into a precise linguistic analysis of the Quranic word 'كلم'. The core usul lesson lies in understanding how Hanafi scholars classify 'كلم' as a noun of genus, not a plural. This distinction affects how we interpret similar words in legal texts and demonstrates the importance of lexical categories in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection on pronoun referent
The objector argues: If the book begins with 'بسم الله', the pronoun in 'إليه' finds a referent in 'الله', so no problem. The response shows that the basmalah may be uttered, kept in heart, or written as blessings without being part of the text, so the referent is not actually mentioned in the book.
This background sets up why the subsequent linguistic analysis is needed.
2
Identify the linguistic claim about 'كلم'
The passage claims that 'كلم' is a noun of genus (اسم جنس) similar to 'تمر' for dates. It is lexically singular but semantically plural, unlike a true plural which is a different morphological category.
The key is the singular lexical form while referring to many instances.
3
Apply the adjective agreement rule
In Arabic, non-intelligent plurals take feminine adjectives (e.g., 'نخل خاوية'). Since the adjective in 'الكلم الطيب' is masculine ('الطيب'), the word 'كلم' must be lexically singular, thus a noun of genus.
This rule is a standard tool in Hanafi usul for discerning lexical categories.
4
Refute the opposing view that 'كلم' is a plural
Some scholars thought 'كلم' is a plural of 'كلمة' because it is often used for many. The author counters that the measure 'فعل' (with kasra on 'ain) is not among plural measures, so it cannot be a true plural.
This shows the importance of morphological patterns (أوزان الجمع) in usul analysis.
5
Conclude the usul principle
Words like 'كلم' are genus nouns: lexically singular, semantically plural. This affects how they are used in legal texts, e.g., adjective agreement and interpretation of commands.
Memorize this concept for future analyses of words like 'تمر', 'شجر', etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلاصہ سوال یہ کہ متن کی ابتداء اگر بالتسمیہ ہے تو اضمار قبل الذکر لازم نہیں آتی کیونکہ تسمیہ میں لفظ اللہ مذکور ہے جو الیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع بن سکتا ہے اگر ابتداء بالتسمیہ نہیں کی تو پھر حدیث کے ساتھ عمل کرنا متروک ہو گا جو شرعا یہ قبیح امر ہے ۔ لانا نقول سے اس کا جواب دیا اور شق اول اختیار کی کہ حدیث پر عمل کرتے ہوئے متن کی ابتداء بالتسمیہ کی گئی ہے لیکن اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ مرجع مذكور في الكتاب ہو کیونکہ ابتداء بالتسميه کی مختلف صورتیں ہو سکتی ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ ابتداء میں تسمیہ کا صرف ذکر لسانی کر لیا جائے دوسرا یہ کہ مخطور في القلب اور مستحضر فی الجنان کے لیا جائے تیسرا یہ کہ ابتدا بکتابت التسمیہ کر لیا جائے لیکن یہ کتابت بقصد تبرک ہو اور تسمیہ کو جز و کتاب نہ بنایا جائے ان تینوں صورتوں میں مرجع مذکور فی الکتاب نہ ہوا پہلی دو صورتوں میں تو ظاہر ہے۔ آخری صورت میں اگرچہ کتابت تسمیہ کتاب میں تو ہوگی لیکن چونکہ وہ کتاب کا حصہ اور جز نہیں ہے تو مرجع کتاب میں مذکور نہ ہوا لہذا اضمار قبل ذكر المرجع فی الکتاب ہر صورت میں لازم آتا ہے ۔ والصعود یعنی صعود کا معنی ہوتا ہے اسفل سے قدر او مرتبہ کے لئے والکام من الكلمة یعنی لفظ کلم کی نسبت الی لفظ الکلمۃ ایسے ہے جیسے نسبتہ تم الی التمرة تو جیسے تم اسم جنس برائے تمرہ ہے اور جنس بغیر تا کے واحد بالتا مستعمل ہے اسی طرح کلمتہ واحد ہے جو بالتا ہے اور کلم جو بغیر تا کے ہے وہ اس کے لئے درجہ جنس میں ہے جو قلیل اور کثیر پر صادق آسکتی ہے اس معنی جنسی کے لحاظ سے اسے جمع کہا جاتا ہے اور لفظا یہ مفرد ہے اور معنی جمع ہے جانب لفظ کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس کی وصف مذکر لائی جا سکتی ہے جیسے نخل منقعر اور جانب معنیٰ کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس کی وصف میں تانیث اختیار کی جا سکتی ہے جیسے سنخل خاویہ کیونکہ جمع غیر ذوی العقول کی صفت مؤنث آتی ہے چونکہ لفظ اسخاص کی بھی حالت وہ کیفیت بطرف نخلہ کے ایسے ہے جیسے تمر کی بنسبت تمرہ کے پھر چونکہ لفظ کلم کی استعمالِ غالب کثیر میں ہوتی ہے ایک دو پر اس کی استعمال نہیں ہے اس لئے بعض حضرات کو تو ہم ہوا کہ یہ جمع ہے کلمہ کی اور تمر و تمرہ کی طرح اس کی حالت جنس اور واحد کی نہیں ہے لیکن حقیقت حال وہی ہے جو واضح ہو چکی ہے اور الکلم الطیب میں تذکیر وصف اسی امر پر دال ہے کہ لفظ کلم اسم جنس ہو کہ لفظ مفرد ہے اور معنی جمع ہے کیونکہ وزن فعل بكسر العین اوزان جمع میں سے نہیں ہے لہذا لفظاً اسے جمع قرار نہیں دیا جا سکتا ۔ فلا ينبغي ان يشك آن یعنی اس مسئلہ میں شک کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے کہ لفظ کلم جمع ہے جیسے
Summary of the objection: If the text begins with 'بسم الله', then 'اضمار قبل الذكر' is not necessary because the word 'الله' is mentioned in the basmalah, which can be the referent of the pronoun in 'إليه'. If it does not begin with basmalah, then acting upon the hadith is abandoned, which is a detestable thing in Shariah. 'لنا أن نقول' answers it, and he chooses the first option: that the text begins with basmalah in accordance with the hadith, but it does not necessitate that the referent is mentioned in the book, because there are different forms of beginning with basmalah. One: only verbal mention of the basmalah at the beginning. Second: that it is hidden in the heart and present in the mind. Third: that one writes the basmalah at the beginning, but this writing is for blessings and the basmalah is not made a part of the book. In all three forms, the referent is not mentioned in the book; the first two are obvious. In the last form, although the writing of the basmalah is in the book, since it is not part or portion of the book, the referent is not mentioned in the book. Thus, 'اضمار قبل ذكر المرجع' in the book is necessary in every case. 'والصعود': The meaning of 'صعود' is movement from lower to a thing that is high and elevated in terms of place and direction. Since here it is 'صعود إلى الله', and Allah is free from place and directions, it is used metaphorically for direction to the high rank or status. 'والكلام من الكلمة': The relationship of the word 'كلم' to the word 'كلمة' is like the relationship of 'تمر' to 'تمرة'. Just as 'تمر' is a noun of genus for 'تمرة', and the genus without 'تاء' is a singular with 'تاء', similarly 'كلمة' is a singular with 'تاء', and 'كلم' without 'تاء' is in the level of genus, which can apply to few and many. In this generic sense, it is called plural, but lexically it is singular and semantically plural. Considering the lexical aspect, its adjective can be masculine, like 'نخل منقعر', and considering the semantic aspect, its adjective can take feminine, like 'نخل خاوية', because the adjective of a non-intelligent plural comes feminine. The state of the word 'اسخاص'? also is similar to 'نخلة' in relation to 'نخل', like 'تمر' in relation to 'تمرة'. Then, since the predominant use of 'كلم' is for many, not for one or two, some scholars have thought it is a plural of 'كلمة', and its state is not that of genus and singular like 'تمر' and 'تمرة'. But the reality is as has become clear: the masculine adjective in 'الكلم الطيب' indicates that the word 'كلم' is a noun of genus, lexically singular and semantically plural, because the measure 'فعل' (with kasra on the 'ain) is not among the measures of the plural. Hence, lexically it cannot be considered a plural. So one should not doubt this: that the word 'كلم' is plural like...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage continues the hashiya, addressing a further objection: If the book begins with 'بسم الله', doesn't that provide a referent for the pronoun? The response clarifies that the basmalah may be uttered verbally, kept in the heart, or written for blessings without being part of the book, so the referent is still not explicitly in the text. The passage then provides a linguistic analysis of the word 'كلم' from the Quranic phrase 'الكلم الطيب'. It explains that 'كلم' is a singular noun indicating a genus (like 'تمر' for dates), not a plural. This is supported by the masculine adjective 'الطيب' (since non-intelligent plurals take feminine adjectives). The author concludes that one should not doubt that 'كلم' is a collective noun, not a plural. This analysis is rooted in Hanafi usul's attention to linguistic precision in interpreting legal texts.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The phrase 'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم' used at the beginning of books.
كلم (kalam): A singular noun in the sense of a genus, meaning 'speech' or 'words', lexically singular but semantically plural.
جنس (jins): A genus noun that applies to individuals, similar to 'تمر' for dates.
اسم جنس (ism al-jins): A noun that denotes a genus or kind; it is lexically singular but can refer to many individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is 'الكلم الطيب' described with a masculine adjective ('الطيب')?
A) Because 'الكلم' is a plural of non-intelligent beings, which takes a masculine adjective.
B) Because 'الكلم' is lexically singular (a noun of genus), and the adjective agrees with its lexical form.
C) Because the referent 'الله' is masculine.
D) Because the adjective 'طيب' is always masculine.

Key Takeaway
The word 'كلم' is a singular noun of genus, not a plural—its masculine adjective and morphological pattern prove this, a key insight in Hanafi usul for lexical classification.

Tadmin: The Linguistic Principle Defending the Preposition 'Fi' in 'Awda'a'
Textual analysis and critical refinement of a prepositional usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle of tadmin and apply it to justify the use of a preposition with a verb that is normally transitive without it.

Core Idea
A verb can borrow another verb's meaning, and with it, its preposition—this is tadmin.

In this passage, we see a classic Hanafi usul debate: the author uses 'fi' with 'awda'a', but the commentator objects because 'awda'a' is normally directly transitive. The Hanafi response invokes tadmin, showing that 'awda'a' here implies 'idraj' (insertion) which takes 'fi'. This lesson unpacks this linguistic tool and its role in text interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic problem
Recognize that the verb 'awda'a' (to deposit) is normally transitive to two objects without a preposition, but the author uses it with the preposition 'fi'.
The first pronoun refers to 'asrar' (secrets) and the second to 'mutashabihat' (ambiguous verses).
2
Recognize the commentator's objection
The commentator claims the author's usage is a leniency (tasamuh) because 'awda'a' should not need a preposition.
The commentator consistently objects to the author's prepositional choices.
3
Apply the principle of tadmin
Understand that 'awda'a' here implies the meaning of 'idraj' (insertion) or 'wad'' (placing), which do require 'fi'.
Tadmin is a broad Arabic linguistic device accepted in Hanafi usul.
4
Justify the usage
The use of 'fi' is not a leniency but a deliberate indication of the implied meaning, making the author's expression sound and correct.
The commentator's objection is refuted as an excess.
5
Conclude the soundness of the author's position
The Hanafi approach validates the author's usage via tadmin, demonstrating flexibility in interpreting sacred texts.
This principle is crucial for understanding how Hanafi scholars handle linguistic nuances in Quran and Hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اودعها فيها پہلی ضمیر اسرار کی طرف اور ثانی متشابہات کی طرف راجع ہے ای اور ع الله الاسرار في المتشابهات والايداع شارح کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ لفظ ابداع دونوں مفاعیل کی طرف بلا واسطہ حرف جر متعدی ہوتا ہے لہذا مصنف کا تعدیہ فی کے ساتھ تسامح ہے اور شارح ہمیشہ مصنف پر صلہ جات میں تسامح کا اعتراض کرتا ہے حالانکہ عرب میں تضمین کا باب وسیع ہے یہاں بھی ایسے ہے کہ ابداع معنی ادراج اور وضع کو متضمن ہے اس لئے لفظ فی لاکر اس تضمین کی طرف اشارہ کیا یہی توجیہ اسلم اور صواب ہے تسامح کا ذکر من الشارح ایک قسم کی زیادتی ہے۔
His statement: 'awda'aha fiha' - the first pronoun refers to 'asrar' and the second refers to 'mutashabihat', meaning 'and Allah placed the secrets in the mutashabihat'. The intent of the commentator is that the word 'ibda' is transitive to two objects without the mediation of a preposition, so the author's using 'fi' is a leniency (tasamuh). The commentator always objects to the author regarding leniencies in prepositions, even though in Arabic the door of tadmin (implication) is wide. Here too, it is such that 'ibda' includes the meaning of 'idraj' and 'wad', so the letter 'fi' was brought to indicate this tadmin. This explanation is sounder and more correct. The mention of tasamuh from the commentator is a kind of excess.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis and critical refinement of the author's use of the preposition 'fi' with the verb 'awda'a'. The commentator objects that the verb 'awda'a' should be transitive directly without a preposition, calling the author's usage a leniency. However, the author's defense invokes the broad Arabic principle of 'tadmin' (implication), where a word implies the meaning of another verb that governs the preposition. Here, 'awda'a' implies the sense of 'idraj' (insertion) or 'wad'' (placing), which normally take 'fi'. Therefore, the author's usage is correct and the commentator's criticism is itself an excess. This demonstrates a key Hanafi usul principle: linguistic flexibility via tadmin is acceptable in interpreting Quranic and hadith texts.

Key Terms
تضمین (tadmin): A word implying the meaning of another word, thereby taking its transitivity or preposition.
تسامح (tasamuh): Leniency or laxity in linguistic usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What linguistic principle does the author use to justify the preposition 'fi' with 'awda'a'?
A) Istihsan (juristic preference)
B) Tadmin (implication)
C) Taqyid (restriction)
D) Naskh (abrogation)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of tadmin allows a verb to take the preposition of an implied meaning, defending seemingly irregular constructions.

Definition of Asl (Foundation) in Usul al-Fiqh
Defines the term 'asl' as that upon which something else is built.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'asl' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and distinguish its sensory and intellectual applications.

Core Idea
The term 'asl' ('foundation') in usul al-fiqh refers to anything upon which something else is built, whether physical or rational.

Every discipline begins with defining its key terms. In usul al-fiqh, the compound 'usul al-fiqh' means the foundations of fiqh, so we must first understand the meaning of 'asl' (foundation). This lesson unpacks the definition of 'asl' as given by a classical author and expanded by his commentator, showing that it encompasses both physical foundations (like a roof on a wall) and intellectual foundations (like a ruling on its evidence). This broad understanding is crucial for legal reasoning, especially in qiyas and source hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and its definitional structure
The author defines 'al-asl' using the idafi (construct) phrase 'ma yabni 'alayhi ghayruhu' – that upon which something else is built. Recognize that the definition uses a relative phrase, which immediately ties 'asl' to something else (the ghayr).
The phrase 'ma yabni 'alayhi ghayruhu' is a formal definition in Arabic: mawṣūf + ṣila.
2
Parse the two types of 'bina' (building): sensory and intellectual
The commentator clarifies that 'bina' includes both sensory (ibtinā’ ḥissī) – like a roof on walls – and intellectual (ibtinā’ ‘aqlī) – like a ruling depending on its evidence. List examples of each from the text.
You know you have understood this when you can give your own example of an intellectual 'asl' (e.g., the Quran as the 'asl' for a ruling).
3
Connect the definition to the compound 'usul al-fiqh'
The commentator explains that a compound definition requires defining its components. 'Usul al-fiqh' = 'usul' (foundations) + 'fiqh' (understanding). The definition of 'usul' depends on knowing what an 'asl' is, which this passage provides.
In Hanafi usul, 'asl' is also used in qiyas to denote the original case (al-asl) from which the ruling is extended.
4
Apply the definition to usul al-fiqh examples
Think of practical examples: the Quran is an 'asl' for rulings; a valid analogy must have a clear 'asl'. The definition here equips you to identify 'asl' in various contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال المصنف الاصل چونکہ تعریف اضافی میں مضاف اور مضاف الیہ دونوں کی تعریف ضروری ہے اس لئے اولاً مضاف کی تعریف کرتے ہوئے کہا الاصل ما بتنی علیہ غیرہ یعنی اصل ایسی شئی کا نام ہے جس پر اس کا غیر یعنی دوسری چیز مبنی ہو یہ ابتناء ابتنار حسی کو شامل ہونا تو ظاہر ہے جیسے ابتنار سقف على الجدران اور اسی طرح ابتنا، عقلی کو بھی شامل ہے جیسے مصنف نے اس کی مثال ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ سے دی ہے۔ قال الشارح قوله اما تعريفها باعتبار الاضافة يعني تعريف اضافی تعریف مضاف جو کہ لفظ اصول ہے اور تعریف مضاف الیہ جو کہ لفظ الفقہ ہے کی طرف محتاج ہے کیونکہ تعریف المرکب اپنے اجزار ترکیبیہ اور مفردات کی تعریف کی طرف محتاج ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ معرفت کل معرفت اجزاء پر موقوف ہوتی ہے لہذا جوا جزا غیر بینہ ہوں ان کی تعریف ضروری ہو جاتی ہے اور جیسے مضافین کی تعریف ضروری ہے اسی طرح
Then the author said: 'al-asl' - because in the idafi definition, both the first part (mudaf) and the second part (mudaf ilayh) need definition. Therefore, first defining the mudaf, he said: 'Al-asl is that upon which something else is built.' That is, 'asl' is the name of a thing upon which its other (i.e., another thing) is based. This 'bina' (construction) includes sensory building, as in the construction of a roof on walls, and similarly includes intellectual building, as the author gave the example of the dependence of a ruling on its evidence. The commentator said: his saying 'now its definition with respect to the idafa' means the idafi definition needs the definition of the mudaf, which is the word 'usul', and the definition of the mudaf ilayh, which is the word 'fiqh', because the definition of a compound needs the definition of its component parts and individual words. Because knowledge of the whole depends on knowledge of the parts. Therefore, when the parts are not clear, their definition becomes necessary. And just as the definition of the two parts of the idafa is necessary, similarly...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'asl' (foundation) within the context of the idafi definition of usul al-fiqh. Since the compound 'usul al-fiqh' consists of 'usul' (plural of 'asl') and 'fiqh', the author must define both. He first defines 'asl' as 'that upon which something else is built.' This definition is broad, encompassing both physical foundations (like a roof resting on walls) and intellectual foundations (like a ruling being based on its evidence). The commentator (al-Sharih) explains that the definition of a compound requires defining its parts, especially if the parts are not self-evident. Thus, defining 'asl' is necessary for understanding 'usul al-fiqh'. The passage demonstrates the usul methodology of defining key terms precisely, and it shows that 'asl' can refer to both sensory and rational foundations, which is important in legal reasoning (e.g., a hadith as an 'asl' for a ruling).

Key Terms
اصل (aṣl): That upon which something else is built; includes both physical and intellectual foundations.
ابتناء حسی (ibtinā’ ḥissī): Sensory/physical construction, e.g., a roof on walls.
ابتناء عقلی (ibtinā’ ‘aqlī): Intellectual construction, e.g., a ruling based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does the term 'asl' (اصل) mean?
A) A physical foundation like a wall.
B) That upon which something else is built, including both sensory and intellectual foundations.
C) The evidence (dalil) for a ruling.
D) The subject matter of a science.

Key Takeaway
In usul al-fiqh, 'asl' is a foundational term that includes both sensory and intellectual bases, essential for understanding legal derivation.

Conditions of a Valid Definition: Tard and 'Aks
Explaining the essential conditions of tard and 'aks for valid definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions of tard and 'aks and apply them to evaluate whether a definition is valid.

Core Idea
Tard ensures coverage; 'aks ensures exclusivity — together they validate a definition.

In usul al-fiqh, a valid definition must precisely capture the defined term. Two logical conditions—tard and 'aks—guarantee that a definition neither leaves out any instance nor includes foreign elements. This lesson unpacks these conditions as explained in the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Recognize that the definition (had) aims to define a concept (mahdud). The conditions apply to any definition, real or nominal.
The passage states 'condition for both definitions, i.e., the real and the nominal.'
2
Extract the condition of tard
Tard means the definition applies to every individual where the defined applies. It ensures comprehensiveness (jam').
Author translates: 'wherever the definition is found, the defined is found.'
3
Extract the condition of 'aks
'Aks is the converse: wherever the defined applies, the definition applies. It ensures exclusivity (man').
Two interpretations: conventional conversion and negative conversion (absence of definition implies absence of defined).
4
See violation examples
If tard is violated, the definition includes non-defined items. If 'aks is violated, the definition excludes some defined items.
Example: if 'human is laughing' and a non-human laughs, tard fails.
5
Apply to evaluate a definition
Given a definition, check both conditions: does it cover all instances? Does it cover only those instances?
This is the parsing exercise from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله شرط لكل التعريفين اى الحقيقى والاسمى الطرد والعكس المنع والجمع اما الطرد فهو یعنی طرد صدق محدود علی ما صدق علیہ الحد صدقاً کلیاً کا نام ہے یعنی ہر وہ مقام جہاں جہاں صادق آئے گی وہاں محدود کا صادق آنا ضروری ہے یہی مراد ہے اس قول معروف کی کلما وجد الحد وجد المحدود قبالا طراد یعنی مرد کے ساتھ حد میں منعیت آجاتی ہے حد مانع عن دخول الغیر ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ جہاں جاتا حد پہنچی تو وہاں محدود کا پہنچنا ضروری ہوا تو اس صورت میں حد غیر محدود پر صادق نہ آئی اگر طرد منتقض ہو جائے مثلاً کسی ایک مقام پر صادق آچکی ہے لیکن محدود وہاں موجود نہیں ہے تو لا محالہ یہ صدغیر می رود پر صادق ہوگی تو مانع عن دخول الغير نہ رہی واما العكس فاخذه از عکس سے مراد کس طرد با عتبار متفاہم عرف کے لیا گیا ہے اور وہ یہ کہ محمول کو موضوع اور موضوع کو محمول بنا لیا جائے اور کمیت سابقہ بعینها بر قرار رکھی جائے یہ عرفی عکس کلیہ کا کلیہ آئے گا جیسے کہا جاتا ہے کل انسان ضاحک و بالعکس ای کل ضاحک انسان اور کہتے ہیں کل انسان حیوان و لا عکس ای لیس کل حیوان انسانا تو یہ ہے عکس عرفی ورنہ تو عکس مجھے موجبہ کلیہ کا موجبہ جزئیہ آتا ہے وہ تو کل انسان حیوان کا صحیح آتا ہے اس لئے مصنف نے بھی اسی بنیاد پر کس کا ترجمہ کل ماصدق علیہ المحدود صدق علیہ اخذ کیا حاصل یہ کہ طرد کے اندر محدود کا حکم کلی علی الحمد کیا جاتا ہے اور عکس کے اندر حد کا حکم کلی علی المحدود ہوتا ہے وبعضهم اخذہ یعنی بعض حضرات نے عکس کو اس مشہور معنی یعنی عکس الاثبات النفی کے لحاظ سے لیا ہے تو اس لحاظ سے مکس کا مفہوم ہوگا کلما انتفى الحد انتقى المحدود یعنی جہاں حد صادق نہ آوے وہاں محدود بھی صادق نہ آوے کیونکہ اگر محدود صادق
He said: condition for both definitions, i.e., the real and the nominal, are tard (comprehensiveness) and 'aks (exclusivity), man' (prevention) and jam' (combination). As for tard, it means: tard is the name for the definition applying to all that the defined applies to, universally. That is, every place where the definition applies, the defined must necessarily apply. This is the meaning of the well-known statement: 'Wherever the definition is found, the defined is found.' In contrast, tard: with the definition, prevention comes; the definition becomes a preventer of the entry of other things, because wherever the definition reaches, the defined necessarily reaches, so in that case the definition does not apply to what is not the defined. If tard is violated, e.g., if the definition applies in some place but the defined is not present there, then inevitably this definition applies to something other than the defined, so it would not remain a preventer of the entry of other things. As for 'aks, it is taken from 'aks in the sense of reciprocal conversion according to common understanding. That is, the predicate is made the subject and the subject is made the predicate, while maintaining the same quantity. This conventional 'aks will yield a universal from a universal, e.g., it is said: 'Every human is laughing' and conversely, i.e., 'Every laughing thing is human.' And they say: 'Every human is an animal' but not conversely, i.e., 'Not every animal is a human.' This is the conventional 'aks. Otherwise, the logical 'aks of a universal affirmative is a particular affirmative, and that is correct for 'Every human is an animal.' For this reason, the author translated 'aks as 'Every individual of which the defined is true, the definition is true of it.' The conclusion: in tard, the ruling of the defined is made universal over the definition, and in 'aks, the ruling of the definition is made over the defined. Some scholars have taken 'aks in the well-known meaning, i.e., the converse of affirmation and negation. In this sense, the meaning of 'aks is: wherever the definition does not apply, the defined also does not apply. Because if the defined applies...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage explains the two essential conditions for a valid definition, whether real or nominal: tard and 'aks. The author states these as conditions, and the commentator elaborates. Tard means that the definition must be coextensive with the defined: wherever the definition applies, the defined must also apply. This ensures the definition is comprehensive (all individuals of the defined are covered). If tard is violated (e.g., the definition applies to something that is not the defined), then the definition fails to exclude others. 'Aks is the converse condition: wherever the defined applies, the definition must also apply. This ensures exclusivity (no non-instances are included). The commentator distinguishes two interpretations of 'aks: one according to conventional usage (common among logicians), which treats 'aks as a simple conversion preserving quantity (universal to universal), and another according to some scholars who take 'aks as the converse of affirmation and negation (i.e., if the definition is absent, the defined is absent). The commentator notes that the author of the matn understood 'aks in the first sense, translating it as 'every individual of which the defined is true, the definition is true of it.' The passage also mentions that tard and 'aks together imply man' (prevention, i.e., the definition prevents non-defined from entering) and jam' (combination, i.e., the definition combines all instances of the defined).

Key Terms
الطرد (al-tard): The condition that the definition applies to every individual of the defined: wherever the definition is true, the defined is true.
العکس (al-'aks): The condition that the definition applies only to individuals of the defined: wherever the defined is true, the definition is true (or conversely, depending on interpretation).
المنع و الجمع (al-man' wa al-jam'): Combined effect of tard and 'aks: the definition prevents non-defined from entering (man') and gathers all instances of the defined (jam').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The condition that a definition must apply to all instances of the defined is called:
A) 'Aks
B) Tard
C) Man'
D) Jam'

Key Takeaway
A valid definition in usul al-fiqh must satisfy both tard (comprehensiveness) and 'aks (exclusivity) to precisely capture the defined term.

The Meaning of Hukm in the Definition of Fiqh: Customary vs Technical
Debate on the meaning of hukm and classification of rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the customary and technical meanings of hukm and evaluate the Hanafi classification of wujub al-iman.

Core Idea
To avoid redundancy in the definition of fiqh, 'hukm' must be taken in its customary sense (complete relation), not the technical 'address of Allah'.

This passage delves into a nuanced debate within Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the precise meaning of 'hukm' as it appears in the definition of fiqh. The author navigates between the technical term of the usul scholars and the customary linguistic sense, addressing a potential redundancy. The outcome has direct implications for what counts as a shar'i ruling, specifically concerning the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Redundancy Problem
Examine why if 'hukm' is taken in its technical usul sense (address of Allah), the restrictions 'shar'i' and 'amali' in the definition of fiqh become redundant. Understand that the technical sense already implies shar'i and amali, so the restrictions would be pointless.
The redundancy arises because 'shar'i' is inherent in the address of Allah, and 'amali' is inherent in rulings related to actions.
2
Understand the Author's Solution
The author proposes that to avoid redundancy, 'hukm' must be taken in its customary sense: a complete relation between two things, which when known yields tasdiq. This interpretation justifies the restrictions.
The author also permits the technical sense but then reinterprets 'shar'i' to mean 'what depends on the shari'a'.
3
Follow the Reinterpretation for the Technical Sense
When 'hukm' is technical, 'shar'i' is redefined as 'ma yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar'' (what depends on the shari'a). This yields two types: address about what depends on shari'a (e.g., wujub al-salat) and address about what does not depend on shari'a (e.g., wujub al-iman? but actually it depends).
The author initially lists wujub al-iman as non-shar'i but then corrects: the example of non-shar'i is nafs al-iman, not wujub al-iman.
4
Analyze the Objection and Response
An objector argues that wujub al-iman should be non-shar'i because shari'a depends on iman. The Hanafi response: shari'a depends on actual faith, not its obligation. Therefore, wujub al-iman is shar'i (depends on shari'a), while nafs al-iman is non-shar'i.
This distinction prevents circular reasoning and clarifies the scope of fiqh.
5
Identify the Final Classification
The passage concludes that shar'i rulings (in the sense of depending on shari'a) are of two types: theoretical (nazari) and practical ('amali). The restriction 'amali' in the definition of fiqh excludes theoretical ones like the proof of consensus.
The commentator notes that technical hukm may not include theoretical at all, making the exclusion redundant on that view.

Source Text

اصول کا مراد ہونا جائز قرار دیا ہے یعنی خطاب اللہ الو پھر چونکہ اس صورت میں شرعیہ وغیرہ کی قید لغو ہو جاتی تھی اس لئے فوائد قیود کی تبیین میں ارتکاب تکلف کیا اور مراد قوم کی توضیح میں ارتکاب تعسف کیا تو مصنف نے اس وقت شرعیہ سے مراد ما يتوقف على الشرع متعین کی یعنی ایسے احکام جن کا علم و ادراک خطاب شارع کے بغیر حاصل ہی نہیں ہو سکتا تو اس صورت میں حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ دو قسم ہوا ایک خطاب بما
